Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Previous scriptures (Torah and Gospel) are sufficient guidance for all people, so there is no need for a new universal prophet.
Correction: The author argues that those scriptures were either guidance before the Quran or they guide people to believe in Muhammad and follow his Sharia, as they contain prophecies about him.

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the author gives for the universal mission of Prophet Muhammad?
A) The Prophet's claim supported by miracles and Quranic verses
B) The consensus of the Companions
C) The fact that he was sent to the Arabs only
D) The Torah and Gospel were abrogated

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad's universal prophethood is proven by his clear claim, miraculous signs, and Quranic testimony; previous scriptures actually pointed to him and are abrogated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though the message of Prophet Muhammad ﷺ is for you personally, or do you sometimes act as if it applies more to others—those who are 'more religious' or from different backgrounds? What would change if you took his universal call as a direct command to your every action today?
?
The passage highlights how even those who claim to follow previous scriptures needed the Prophet because their religion had become corrupted. How might your own understanding of Islam be corrupted by culture, habit, or convenience? Will you seek the unaltered truth from the Quran and Sunnah, even when it challenges your comfort?
?
If the Prophet's prophethood is final and his Sharia is unchangeable, what does that mean for the areas of your life where you have made concessions or compromises, thinking 'it's just a small matter' or 'times have changed'? Will you submit fully, or do you still hold back something?

Jesus Follows Muhammad's Sharia
Answering the objection that Jesus's survival contradicts Muhammad's seal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the continued presence of Jesus (as) does not contradict Muhammad's status as the Seal of the Prophets.

Core Idea
Jesus will return as a follower of Muhammad, not a new prophet.

Some may wonder how Jesus (as) being alive and returning to earth can be reconciled with Muhammad being the final prophet. In this passage, the author addresses this objection directly, clarifying that Jesus will descend according to Muhammad's Sharia and will follow him, just as the Prophet said Moses would have done. This preserves the finality of prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic and translation to see the objection about Jesus's continued existence and the author's answer.
Notice the author does not deny Jesus's life but reinterprets its meaning.
2
Identify the key principle
The author explains that Jesus will follow Muhammad's Sharia, meaning he will not bring a new law.
3
Connect to the Hadith
The author references a hadith where the Prophet said Moses would have followed him if alive. This strengthens the argument.
This analogy shows the continuity of prophethood under Muhammad.
4
Apply the concept
Reflect on how this preserves the meaning of 'Seal of the Prophets' — no new prophet with a new Sharia comes after Muhammad.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : أليس عيسى عليه السلام) حياً بعد نبينا، رفع إلى السماء، وسينزل إلى الدنيا؟ قلنا بلى ولكنه على شريعة نبينا، لا يسعه إلا اتباعه على ما قال (عليه السلام) في حق موسى أنه لو كان حياً لما وسعه إلا اتباعي، فيصح أنه خاتم الأنبياء، بمعنى أنه لا يبعث نبي بعده
If it is said: Is not Jesus (peace be upon him) alive after our Prophet, raised to heaven, and will descend to the earth? We say: Yes, but he is upon the Sharia of our Prophet; he cannot do other than follow him, as he (peace be upon him) said regarding Moses: 'If he were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' So it is correct that he (Muhammad) is the Seal of the Prophets, meaning that no prophet will be sent after him.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding Jesus (as). The objector notes that Jesus is alive after our Prophet and will descend, which might seem to contradict Muhammad being the seal of prophets. The author answers that Jesus will descend but will follow Muhammad's Sharia, just as the Prophet said about Moses that if he were alive, he would follow him. Thus, Muhammad remains the seal in the sense that no new prophet with a new Sharia will come; Jesus will be a follower, not a new prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the return of Jesus contradicts Muhammad's finality as a prophet.
Correction: Jesus will return as a follower of Muhammad's Sharia, not as a bringer of a new law, so Muhammad remains the seal.

Checkpoint

A) Jesus will never descend again
B) Jesus will follow Muhammad's Sharia
C) Jesus is not a prophet
D) Muhammad's seal applies only to prophets with new laws

Key Takeaway
Muhammad remains the Seal of the Prophets because any future prophet, including Jesus, will follow his Sharia, not bring a new one.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
What would change in your life if you truly believed that no new revelation will come after the Quran? How does that certainty shape your urgency in seeking guidance from the Quran and Sunna?
?
The Prophet said that if Moses were alive, he would follow him. Do you have the same humility to submit to the truth, even if it challenges your previous beliefs or pride?

Consensus and Evidences for Muhammad's Superiority
The author states the consensus and lists evidences for Muhammad's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus that Muhammad is the best prophet and the key evidences for his superiority, including his community's excellence and his unique characteristics.

Core Idea
Muhammad's community's excellence proves his own excellence.

In this passage, the author presents the unanimous Muslim consensus that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all prophets. He then provides a range of evidences, from the excellence of his community as stated in the Quran to his unique roles and miracles. This lesson unpacks these proofs and also addresses the Prophet's humility in forbidding comparisons.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow from consensus to evidences.
Note the shift from positive claims to the humility hadith.
2
Identify the primary evidence
Focus on the argument that the excellence of the community implies the excellence of the messenger. Why is this logical?
The Quranic verses about the best community are key.
3
Explore the additional characteristics
List the unique qualities of Muhammad mentioned: sent to jinn and humans, seal of prophets, permanent miracle, abrogating Sharia, testimony over mankind.
These are distinct from the community argument.
4
Understand the humility hadith
The Prophet forbids preferring him over Moses and Jonah out of humility. How does this relate to his superiority?
The author clarifies it does not negate his rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأجمع المسلمون على أن أفضل الأنبياء محمد، لأن أمته خير الأمم لقوله تعالى: كُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلناسِ ) (۱) ﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطَا (٢). وتفضيل الأمة من حيث إنها أمة تفضيل للرسول الذي هم أمته، ولأنه مبعوث إلى الثقلين، وخاتم الأنبياء والرسل ومعجزته الظاهرة الباهرة باقية على وجه الزمان، وشريعته ناسخة لجميع الأديان، وشهادته قائمة في القيامة على كافة البشر، الى غير ذلك من خصائص لا تعد ولا تحصى. وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَفعَ بعضهم دَرَجَاتِ ﴾ (۳) . إشارة إلى ذلك، والأحاديث الصحاح في هذا المعنى كثيرة، حتى قال (عليه السلام : أنا أكرم الأولين والآخرين على الله تعالى ولا فخر. كما قال (عليه السلام): لا تخيروني على موسى، وما ينبغي لعبد أن يقول : إني خير من يونس بن متى تواضع منه
And the Muslims have agreed that the best of the prophets is Muhammad, because his community is the best of communities, by His saying: 'You are the best community brought forth for mankind' (1) 'And thus We have made you a middle community' (2). And the preference of the community insofar as it is a community is a preference for the messenger whose community they are, and because he is sent to the two weighty ones, and the Seal of the Prophets and Messengers, and his manifest and dazzling miracle remains throughout time, and his Sharia abrogates all religions, and his testimony stands on the Day of Resurrection over all mankind, and other countless characteristics. And His saying: 'And We raised some of them above others in degrees' (3) is an indication of that, and the authentic hadiths on this meaning are many, until he (peace be upon him) said: 'I am the most honored of the first and the last with Allah Almighty, and I say this without pride.' And he also said: 'Do not give me superiority over Moses, and it is not befitting for a servant to say that I am better than Jonah son of Matta' — this out of humility.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage presents the consensus that Muhammad is the best of prophets. The evidence includes: his community is the best, as stated in the Quran ('You are the best community'), and the preference of the community implies the preference of the messenger. Additionally, his unique characteristics include being sent to both humans and jinn, being the seal, having a permanent miracle (the Quran), his Sharia abrogating all previous ones, and his testimony over mankind on Judgment Day. The author cites a verse about raising some in degrees and many hadiths, including the Prophet's statement that he is the most honored without pride, and his humbly forbidding people from preferring him over Moses or Jonah.

Key Terms
أفضل الأنبياء
خير أمة
أمة وسطا
خاتم الأنبياء
معجزة باقية
شريعة ناسخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's statement forbidding preference over Moses and Jonah implies he is not superior to them.
Correction: The author clarifies that this was said out of humility (tawadu'), not as a denial of his actual rank.

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence given for Muhammad being the best prophet?
A) His community is the best community
B) He is the seal of the prophets
C) His miracle is permanent
D) He was sent to both humans and jinn

Key Takeaway
The consensus that Muhammad is the best prophet is supported by multiple Quranic and hadith evidences, while his humility serves as a model of character.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that the Prophet, despite being the best of creation, spoke with such humility as to forbid preference over other prophets, what does that expose about the pride that often takes root in your own heart? In what specific situation this week will you consciously lower yourself as he did, not out of false modesty but out of genuine humility before Allah?
?
The Prophet's community is declared the best community. Do you live as a member of that community with the responsibility that comes with that status, or do you take comfort in the label while your actions betray indifference? What one habit must you change today to truly embody being from 'the best community'?
?
The Quran is the permanent miracle that abrogates all previous scriptures. Yet how often do you turn to it as your decisive guide, versus consulting it only when convenient? What would it look like for you to submit completely to the authority of this abrogating Sharia in a specific area of your life that you have been resisting?

Differing Views on the Best Prophet After Muhammad
Enumeration of opinions on the best prophet after Muhammad and Christian claim for Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the internal Islamic disagreements on the most excellent prophet after Muhammad and the Christian argument for Jesus' superiority.

Core Idea
Muslims agree Muhammad is best, but differ on the next; Christians claim Jesus surpasses all.

This passage from Sanusi's Sharh al-Maqasid surveys the various opinions within Islam on who is the best prophet after Muhammad, listing Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, and Jesus with supporting reasons. It then presents the Christian claim that Jesus is superior to all prophets, based on his miraculous birth, purity, and divine titles. Understanding these differing views clarifies the Islamic consensus on Muhammad's primacy and the boundaries of prophetic excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the five opinions and the shift to the Christian argument.
2
Identify the five prophets and their reasons
List each prophet mentioned (Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus) and the specific virtue attributed to them in the text.
For example, Adam is 'father of mankind', Noah has 'long worship', etc.
3
Examine the Christian argument
The passage states that Christians give Jesus superiority because he is 'a word cast to Mary', 'a spirit from Him', pure, not created from sperm, etc. Notice the key phrases.
This argument contrasts with Islamic views.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this discussion matters: it affirms Muhammad's unique status while acknowledging diversity of opinion on secondary rank, and highlights Islamic refutation of Christian exceptionalism.
The author likely continues to refute the Christian claim in the original text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في الأفضل بعده، فقيل : آدم ، لكونه أبا البشر. وقيل: نوح لطول عبادته ومجاهدته . وقيل : إبراهيم لزيادة توكله واطمئنانه . وقيل : موسى، لكونه كليم الله ونجيه . وقيل : عيسى، لكونه روح الله وصفيه . وفضله النصارى على الكل بأنه كلمة ألقاها إلى مريم وروح منه ، طاهر مقدس ، لم يخلق من نطفة، وقد ولدته سيدة نساء العالمين المطهرة عن الأدناس، وتربى في حجر الأنبياء والأولياء، وتكلم
And they differed concerning who is the best after him (Muhammad). It was said: Adam, because he is the father of mankind. And it was said: Noah, due to the length of his worship and his struggle. And it was said: Abraham, due to his increased trust and tranquility. And it was said: Moses, because he is the interlocutor of Allah and His intimate. And it was said: Jesus, because he is the Spirit of Allah and His chosen one. And the Christians gave him superiority over all, (saying) that he is a word cast to Mary and a spirit from Him, pure and holy, not created from a sperm-drop, and the chief of the women of the worlds, purified from impurities, gave birth to him, and he was raised in the lap of the prophets and saints, and he spoke
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage enumerates the different scholarly opinions regarding the best prophet after Muhammad. Some say Adam due to being the father of humanity, others Noah for his long worship, Abraham for his trust, Moses for speaking with Allah, and Jesus for being the Spirit of Allah. Then the author mentions the Christian claim that Jesus is superior to all, based on his miraculous birth, purity, and upbringing. The passage ends mid-sentence ('and he spoke'), but it is clear that the author is presenting and likely refuting this Christian position, as the context of the book is kalam defending Islamic beliefs.

A) Adam
B) Noah

Key Takeaway
The passage shows that Islamic scholarly tradition acknowledges different views on the secondary rank of prophets, but the Christian claim for Jesus' superiority is presented as a contrast to Islamic consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Of the prophets listed (Adam, Noah, Abraham, Moses, Jesus), which one do you feel the closest personal connection to, and what does that say about the virtue you need most in your own life right now?
